<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Intentional act of causing one's own death</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For information on prevention, see <a href="/wiki/Suicide_prevention" title="Suicide prevention">suicide prevention</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Suicide_(disambiguation)" title="Suicide (disambiguation)">suicide (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

</tr><tr><th class="sidebar-heading" style="background:#aaddff; color:#000;">

</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Homicide" title="Template:Homicide"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Homicide" title="Template talk:Homicide"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Homicide&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Suicide</b> is the act of intentionally causing one's own <a href="/wiki/Death" title="Death">death</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sted2006_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sted2006-9">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mental_disorder" title="Mental disorder">Mental disorders</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">depression</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bipolar_disorder" title="Bipolar disorder">bipolar disorder</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autism" title="Autism">autism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Personality_disorder" title="Personality disorder">personality disorders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anxiety_disorder" title="Anxiety disorder">anxiety disorders</a>), physical disorders (such as <a href="/wiki/Chronic_fatigue_syndrome" title="Chronic fatigue syndrome">chronic fatigue syndrome</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Substance_use_disorder" title="Substance use disorder">substance use disorders</a> (including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcohol_use_disorder" title="Alcohol use disorder">alcohol use disorder</a> and the use of and <a href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine_withdrawal_syndrome" title="Benzodiazepine withdrawal syndrome">withdrawal</a> from <a href="/wiki/Benzodiazepine" title="Benzodiazepine">benzodiazepines</a>) are risk factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2016_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2016-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hawton2009_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hawton2009-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Autism2014_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Autism2014-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dod2017_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dod2017-10">[10]</a></sup> Some suicides are impulsive acts due to stress (such as from financial or <a href="/wiki/Suicide_in_colleges_in_the_United_States" title="Suicide in colleges in the United States">academic difficulties</a>), relationship problems (such as <a href="/wiki/Breakup" title="Breakup">breakups</a> or <a href="/wiki/Divorce" title="Divorce">divorces</a>), or harassment and bullying.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2016_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2016-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Those who have previously attempted suicide are at a higher risk for future attempts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2016_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2016-2">[2]</a></sup> Effective <a href="/wiki/Suicide_prevention" title="Suicide prevention">suicide prevention</a> efforts include limiting access to methods of suicide such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Firearms" title="Firearms">firearms</a>, drugs, and poisons; treating mental disorders and substance abuse; careful <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">media</a> reporting about suicide; and improving economic conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2016_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2016-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Crisis_hotline" title="Crisis hotline">crisis hotlines</a> are common resources, their effectiveness has not been well studied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sak2011_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sak2011-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zal2016_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zal2016-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>The most commonly adopted <a href="/wiki/Suicide_methods" title="Suicide methods">method of suicide</a> varies from country to country and is partly related to the availability of effective means.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yip2012_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yip2012-16">[16]</a></sup> Common methods of suicide include hanging, <a href="/wiki/Pesticide_poisoning" title="Pesticide poisoning">pesticide poisoning</a>, and firearms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2016_2-6"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2016-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aj2008_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aj2008-17">[17]</a></sup> Suicides resulted in 828,000 deaths globally in 2015, an increase from 712,000 deaths in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GBD2015De_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-GBD2015De-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GDB2013_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-GDB2013-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Cleanup"><span title='misleading formulation, rate went down by a sixth, which contradicts Epidemiology: "Rates of suicide have increased by 60% from the 1960s to 2012"'>inconsistent</span></a></i>]</sup> This makes suicide the 10th <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leading_cause_of_death" title="Leading cause of death">leading cause of death</a> worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hawton2009_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hawton2009-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>Approximately 1.5% of all deaths worldwide are by suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NEJM2020_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-NEJM2020-8">[8]</a></sup> In a given year, this is roughly 12 per 100,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup> Rates of suicide are generally higher among men than women, ranging from 1.5 times higher in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_World" title="Developing World">developing world</a> to 3.5 times higher in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_World" title="Developed World">developed world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2014Pre_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2014Pre-1">[1]</a></sup> Suicide is generally most common among those over the age of 70; however, in certain countries, those aged between 15 and 30 are at the highest risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2014Pre_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2014Pre-1">[1]</a></sup> Europe had the highest rates of suicide by region in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> There are an estimated 10 to 20 million <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Failed_suicide_attempt" title="Failed suicide attempt">non-fatal attempted suicides</a> every year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Non-fatal suicide attempts may lead to injury and long-term disabilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a>, attempts are more common among young people and women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>Views on suicide have been influenced by broad existential themes such as religion, honor, and the meaning of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Abrahamic_religions" title="Abrahamic religions">Abrahamic religions</a> traditionally consider suicide as an <a href="/wiki/Sin" title="Sin">offense towards God</a> due to the belief in the <a href="/wiki/Sanctity_of_life" title="Sanctity of life">sanctity of life</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">samurai</a> era in Japan, a form of suicide known as <a href="/wiki/Seppuku" title="Seppuku">seppuku</a> (<span title="Japanese-language text"><span lang="ja">腹切り</span></span>, <span title="Japanese-language text"><i lang="ja-Latn">harakiri</i></span>) was respected as a means of making up for failure or as a form of protest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sati_(practice)" title="Sati (practice)">Sati</a>, a practice outlawed by the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British</a> in India, expected a <a href="/wiki/Widow#Widows_in_Indian_culture" title="Widow">Hindu widow</a> to <a href="/wiki/Self-immolation" title="Self-immolation">immolate herself</a> on her husband's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Funeral_pyre" title="Funeral pyre">funeral pyre</a>, either willingly or under pressure from her family and society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Suicide and attempted suicide, while previously illegal, are no longer so in most Western countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-White2010_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-White2010-28">[28]</a></sup> It <a href="#Legislation">remains a criminal offense in some countries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Islam2006_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Islam2006-29">[29]</a></sup> In the 20th and 21st centuries, suicide has been used on rare occasions as a form of protest, and <a href="/wiki/Kamikaze" title="Kamikaze">kamikaze</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suicide_bombings" title="Suicide bombings">suicide bombings</a> have been used as a military or terrorist tactic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Suicide is often seen as a major catastrophe for families, relatives, and other nearby supporters, and it is viewed negatively almost everywhere around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Suicide_terminology" title="Suicide terminology">Suicide terminology</a></div>
<p>Suicide, derived from Latin <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">suicidium</i></span>, is "the act of taking one's own life".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sted2006_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sted2006-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Attempted suicide or non-fatal suicidal behavior amounts to <a href="/wiki/Self-harm" title="Self-harm">self-injury</a> with at least some desire to end one's life that does not result in death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krug2002_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Krug2002-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tur2016_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tur2016-36">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Assisted_suicide" title="Assisted suicide">Assisted suicide</a> occurs when one individual helps another bring about their own death indirectly via providing either advice or the means to the end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gullota2002_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gullota2002-37">[37]</a></sup> This is in contrast to <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">euthanasia</a>, where another person takes a more active role in bringing about a person's death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gullota2002_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gullota2002-37">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Suicidal_ideation" title="Suicidal ideation">Suicidal ideation</a> is thoughts of ending one's life but not taking any active efforts to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krug2002_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-Krug2002-35">[35]</a></sup> It may or may not involve exact planning or intent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tur2016_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tur2016-36">[36]</a></sup> In a <a href="/wiki/Murder%E2%80%93suicide" title="Murder–suicide">murder–suicide</a> (or homicide–suicide), the individual aims at taking the lives of others at the same time. A special case of this is extended suicide, where the murder is motivated by seeing the murdered persons as an extension of their self.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Suicide in which the reason is that the person feels that they are not part of society is known as <a href="/wiki/Suicide_(Durkheim_book)#Egoistic_suicide" title="Suicide (Durkheim book)">egoistic suicide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, the Centre for Suicide Prevention in Canada found that the normal verb in scholarly research and journalism for the act of suicide was <i>commit</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Olsen_2011_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Olsen_2011-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beaton_2013_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beaton_2013-41">[41]</a></sup> On the other hand, the American Psychological Association lists "committed suicide" as a term to avoid because it "frame[s] suicide as a crime".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Some advocacy groups recommend using the terms <i>took his/her own life</i>, <i>died by suicide</i>, or <i>killed him/herself</i> instead of <i>committed suicide</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beck_1974_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beck_1974-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIMH_2001_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIMH_2001-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time_To_Change_2008_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Time_To_Change_2008-45">[45]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associated_Press_Stylebook" title="Associated Press Stylebook">Associated Press Stylebook</a> recommends avoiding "committed suicide" except in direct quotes from authorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">Guardian</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">Observer</a></i> style guides deprecate the use of "committed",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> as does <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Opponents of <i>commit</i> argue that it implies that suicide is criminal, sinful, or morally wrong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ball_2005_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ball_2005-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Risk_factors">Risk factors</span></h2>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:500px; background: white;">
<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
<tbody><tr style="background:#DDD"><th colspan="5" style="text-align:center;">Precipitating circumstances in the US, 2017<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></th></tr>
<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">
<td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">Categories</td>
<td style="width:180px; text-align:left;"></td>

</tr>

<tr><td colspan="5" style="padding:5px; text-align:left;">Suicide is multi-factorial. Multiple precipitating circumstances and risk factors can apply to the same person.</td></tr>
</tbody></table>
</div>
</div>
<p>Factors that affect the risk of suicide include mental disorders, drug misuse, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychological_state" title="Psychological state">psychological states</a>, cultural, family and social situations, genetics, experiences of trauma or loss, and <a href="/wiki/Nihilism" title="Nihilism">nihilism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hawton2012_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hawton2012-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cdc.gov_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-cdc.gov-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zal2016_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zal2016-15">[15]</a></sup> Mental disorders and substance misuse frequently co-exist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drug2011_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Drug2011-53">[53]</a></sup> Other risk factors include having previously attempted suicide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> the ready availability of a means to take one's life, a family history of suicide, or the presence of <a href="/wiki/Traumatic_brain_injury" title="Traumatic brain injury">traumatic brain injury</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> For example, suicide rates have been found to be greater in households with firearms than those without them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miller_393–408_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miller_393–408-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socio-economic" title="Socio-economic">Socio-economic</a> problems such as unemployment, poverty, homelessness, and <a href="/wiki/Discrimination" title="Discrimination">discrimination</a> may trigger suicidal thoughts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Suicide might be rarer in societies with high <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_cohesion" title="Social cohesion">social cohesion</a> and moral objections against suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tur2016_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tur2016-36">[36]</a></sup> About 15–40% of people leave a <a href="/wiki/Suicide_note" title="Suicide note">suicide note</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> War veterans have a higher risk of suicide due in part to higher rates of mental illness, such as <a href="/wiki/Post-traumatic_stress_disorder" title="Post-traumatic stress disorder">post-traumatic stress disorder</a>, and physical health problems related to war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martyr2009_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martyr2009-59">[59]</a></sup> Genetics appears to account for between 38% and 55% of suicidal behaviors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brent2008_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brent2008-60">[60]</a></sup> Suicides may also occur as a local <a href="/wiki/Clustering_(demographics)" title="Clustering (demographics)">cluster</a> of cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2018Risk_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDC2018Risk-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most research does not distinguish between risk factors that lead to thinking about suicide and risk factors that lead to suicide attempts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Risks for suicide attempt rather than just thoughts of suicide include a high pain tolerance and a reduced fear of death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mental_illness">Mental illness</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%27Suicidal_melancholy%27_Wellcome_L0022593_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="833" data-file-width="682" decoding="async" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/%27Suicidal_melancholy%27_Wellcome_L0022593_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-%27Suicidal_melancholy%27_Wellcome_L0022593_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/%27Suicidal_melancholy%27_Wellcome_L0022593_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-%27Suicidal_melancholy%27_Wellcome_L0022593_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/%27Suicidal_melancholy%27_Wellcome_L0022593_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-%27Suicidal_melancholy%27_Wellcome_L0022593_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%27Suicidal_melancholy%27_Wellcome_L0022593_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A picture of a woman with depression, who was suicidal</div></div></div>
<p>Mental illness is present at the time of suicide 27% to more than 90% of the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-University_of_Manchester_Centre_for_Mental_Health_and_Risk_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Manchester_Centre_for_Mental_Health_and_Risk-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Of those who have been hospitalized for suicidal behavior, the lifetime risk of suicide is 8.6%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bos2000_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bos2000-68">[68]</a></sup> Comparatively, non-suicidal people hospitalized for affective disorders have a 4% lifetime risk of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bos2000_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bos2000-68">[68]</a></sup> Half of all people who die by suicide may have <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">major depressive disorder</a>; having this or one of the other <a href="/wiki/Mood_disorder" title="Mood disorder">mood disorders</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Bipolar_disorder" title="Bipolar disorder">bipolar disorder</a> increases the risk of suicide 20-fold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Che2012_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Che2012-69">[69]</a></sup> Other conditions implicated include <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenia</a> (14%), <a href="/wiki/Personality_disorder" title="Personality disorder">personality disorders</a> (8%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Obsessive%E2%80%93compulsive_disorder" title="Obsessive–compulsive disorder">obsessive–compulsive disorder</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Post-traumatic_stress_disorder" title="Post-traumatic stress disorder">post-traumatic stress disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-5"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> Those with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autism" title="Autism">autism</a> also attempt and consider suicide more frequently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>Others estimate that about half of people who die by suicide could be diagnosed with a personality disorder, with <a href="/wiki/Borderline_personality_disorder" title="Borderline personality disorder">borderline personality disorder</a> being the most common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> About 5% of people with <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenia</a> die of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet09_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet09-75">[75]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eating_disorder" title="Eating disorder">Eating disorders</a> are another high risk condition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tint2010_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tint2010-76">[76]</a></sup> Around 22% to 50% of people suffering with gender dysphoria have attempted suicide, however this greatly varies by region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>Among approximately 80% of suicides, the individual has seen a physician within the year before their death,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pir1998_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pir1998-82">[82]</a></sup> including 45% within the prior month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Approximately 25–40% of those who died by suicide had contact with mental health services in the prior year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-University_of_Manchester_Centre_for_Mental_Health_and_Risk_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Manchester_Centre_for_Mental_Health_and_Risk-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pir1998_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pir1998-82">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antidepressant" title="Antidepressant">Antidepressants</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SSRI" title="SSRI">SSRI</a> class appear to increase the frequency of suicide among children but do not change the risk among adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> An unwillingness to get help for mental health problems also increases the risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2018Risk_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDC2018Risk-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Previous_attempts">Previous attempts</span></h3>
<p>A previous history of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suicide_attempts" title="Suicide attempts">suicide attempts</a> is the most accurate predictor of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-6"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> Approximately 20% of suicides have had a previous attempt, and of those who have attempted suicide, 1% die by suicide within a year<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-7"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> and more than 5% die by suicide within 10 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tint2010_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tint2010-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-harm">Self-harm</span></h3>
<p>Non-suicidal self-harm is common with 18% of people engaging in self-harm over the course of their life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 1">: 1 </span></sup> Acts of self-harm are not usually suicide attempts and most who self-harm are not at high risk of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grey2009_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grey2009-86">[86]</a></sup> Some who self-harm, however, do still end their life by suicide, and risk for self-harm and suicide may overlap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grey2009_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-Grey2009-86">[86]</a></sup> Individuals who have been identified as self-harming after being admitted to hospital are <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="6999680000000000000♠"></span>68%</span> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1038841319">.mw-parser-output .tooltip-dotted{border-bottom:1px dotted;cursor:help}</style><span class="rt-commentedText tooltip tooltip-dotted" title="95% confidence interval"><span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7001380000000000000♠"></span>38</span>–<span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7000105000000000000♠"></span>105%</span></span>) more likely to die by suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page: 279">: 279 </span></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Psychosocial_factors">Psychosocial factors</span></h3>
<p>A number of psychological factors increase the risk of suicide including: hopelessness, <a href="/wiki/Anhedonia" title="Anhedonia">loss of pleasure in life</a>, <a href="/wiki/Depression_(mood)" title="Depression (mood)">depression</a>, anxiousness, agitation, rigid thinking, <a href="/wiki/Rumination_(psychology)" title="Rumination (psychology)">rumination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thought_suppression" title="Thought suppression">thought suppression</a>, and poor <a href="/wiki/Coping" title="Coping">coping</a> skills.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Che2012_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Che2012-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ocon2014_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ocon2014-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> A poor ability to solve problems, the loss of abilities one used to have, and poor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Impulse_control" title="Impulse control">impulse control</a> also play a role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Che2012_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-Che2012-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joiner2005_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Joiner2005-90">[90]</a></sup> In older adults, the perception of being a burden to others is important.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Van2011_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Van2011-91">[91]</a></sup> Those who have never married are also at greater risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-8"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> Recent life <a href="/wiki/Psychological_stress" title="Psychological stress">stresses</a>, such as a loss of a family member or friend or the loss of a job, might be a contributing factor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Che2012_69-3"><a href="#cite_note-Che2012-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2018Risk_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-CDC2018Risk-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>Certain personality factors, especially high levels of <a href="/wiki/Neuroticism" title="Neuroticism">neuroticism</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Introverted" title="Introverted">introvertedness</a>, have been associated with suicide. This might lead to people who are isolated and <a href="/wiki/Distress_tolerance" title="Distress tolerance">sensitive to distress</a> to be more likely to attempt suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ocon2014_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ocon2014-88">[88]</a></sup> On the other hand, <a href="/wiki/Optimism" title="Optimism">optimism</a> has been shown to have a protective effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ocon2014_88-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ocon2014-88">[88]</a></sup> Other psychological risk factors include having few reasons for living and feeling trapped in a stressful situation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ocon2014_88-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ocon2014-88">[88]</a></sup> Changes to the stress response system in the brain might be altered during suicidal states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tur2016_36-3"><a href="#cite_note-Tur2016-36">[36]</a></sup> Specifically, changes in the <a href="/wiki/Polyamine" title="Polyamine">polyamine</a> system<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hypothalamic%E2%80%93pituitary%E2%80%93adrenal_axis" title="Hypothalamic–pituitary–adrenal axis">hypothalamic–pituitary–adrenal axis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Social_isolation" title="Social isolation">Social isolation</a> and the lack of <a href="/wiki/Social_support" title="Social support">social support</a> has been associated with an increased risk of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ocon2014_88-4"><a href="#cite_note-Ocon2014-88">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">Poverty</a> is also a factor,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stark2011_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stark2011-94">[94]</a></sup> with heightened relative poverty compared to those around a person increasing suicide risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Over 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Farmers%27_suicides_in_India" title="Farmers' suicides in India">farmers in India have died by suicide</a> since 1997, partly due to issues of debt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> In China, suicide is three times as likely in rural regions as urban ones, partly, it is believed, due to financial difficulties in this area of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>The time of year may also affect suicide rates. There appears to be a decrease around Christmas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> but an increase in rates during spring and summer, which might be related to exposure to sunshine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tur2016_36-4"><a href="#cite_note-Tur2016-36">[36]</a></sup> Another study found that the risk may be greater for males on their birthday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p>Being religious may reduce one's risk of suicide while beliefs that suicide is noble may increase it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Religion2009_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Religion2009-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2018Risk_61-3"><a href="#cite_note-CDC2018Risk-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> This has been attributed to the negative stance many religions take against suicide and to the greater connectedness religion may give.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Religion2009_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-Religion2009-100">[100]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>, among religious people, appear to have a lower rate of suicide; however, the data supporting this is not strong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Islam2006_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Islam2006-29">[29]</a></sup> There does not appear to be a difference in rates of attempted suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Islam2006_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-Islam2006-29">[29]</a></sup> Young women in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> may have higher rates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Substance_misuse">Substance misuse</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Drunkard%27s_Progress_1846.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3905" data-file-width="5330" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/The_Drunkard%27s_Progress_1846.jpg/300px-The_Drunkard%27s_Progress_1846.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/The_Drunkard%27s_Progress_1846.jpg/450px-The_Drunkard%27s_Progress_1846.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/The_Drunkard%27s_Progress_1846.jpg/600px-The_Drunkard%27s_Progress_1846.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Drunkard%27s_Progress_1846.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"The Drunkard's Progress", 1846 demonstrating how alcoholism can lead to poverty, crime, and eventually suicide</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Substance_misuse" title="Substance misuse">Substance misuse</a> is the second most common risk factor for suicide after major depression and bipolar disorder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Both chronic substance misuse as well as <a href="/wiki/Substance_intoxication" title="Substance intoxication">acute intoxication</a> are associated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drug2011_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Drug2011-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fadem2004_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fadem2004-104">[104]</a></sup> When combined with personal grief, such as <a href="/wiki/Grief" title="Grief">bereavement</a>, the risk is further increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fadem2004_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fadem2004-104">[104]</a></sup> Substance misuse is also associated with mental health disorders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drug2011_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-Drug2011-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most people are under the influence of <a href="/wiki/Sedative" title="Sedative">sedative-hypnotic drugs</a> (such as alcohol or benzodiazepines) when they die by suicide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Youssef2008_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Youssef2008-105">[105]</a></sup> with alcoholism present in between 15% and 61% of cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drug2011_53-3"><a href="#cite_note-Drug2011-53">[53]</a></sup> Use of prescribed benzodiazepines is associated with an increased rate of suicide and attempted suicide. The pro-suicidal effects of benzodiazepines are suspected to be due to a psychiatric disturbance caused by side effects, such as <a href="/wiki/Disinhibition" title="Disinhibition">disinhibition</a>, or withdrawal symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dod2017_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dod2017-10">[10]</a></sup> Countries that have higher rates of alcohol use and a greater density of bars generally also have higher rates of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ETOH2006_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-ETOH2006-106">[106]</a></sup> About 2.2–3.4% of those who have been treated for alcoholism at some point in their life die by suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ETOH2006_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-ETOH2006-106">[106]</a></sup> Alcoholics who attempt suicide are usually male, older, and have tried to take their own lives in the past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drug2011_53-4"><a href="#cite_note-Drug2011-53">[53]</a></sup> Between 3 and 35% of deaths among those who use <a href="/wiki/Heroin" title="Heroin">heroin</a> are due to suicide (approximately fourteenfold greater than those who do not use).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> In adolescents who misuse alcohol, neurological and psychological dysfunctions may contribute to the increased risk of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid17458319_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid17458319-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>The misuse of <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Methamphetamine" title="Methamphetamine">methamphetamine</a> has a high correlation with suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drug2011_53-5"><a href="#cite_note-Drug2011-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In those who use cocaine, the risk is greatest during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cocaine_withdrawal" title="Cocaine withdrawal">withdrawal phase</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Those who used <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inhalant_abuse" title="Inhalant abuse">inhalants</a> are also at significant risk with around 20% attempting suicide at some point and more than 65% considering it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drug2011_53-6"><a href="#cite_note-Drug2011-53">[53]</a></sup> Smoking cigarettes is associated with risk of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hughes2008_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hughes2008-111">[111]</a></sup> There is little evidence as to why this association exists; however, it has been hypothesized that those who are predisposed to smoking are also predisposed to suicide, that smoking causes health problems which subsequently make people want to end their life, and that smoking affects brain chemistry causing a propensity for suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hughes2008_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hughes2008-111">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">Cannabis</a>, however, does not appear to independently increase the risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drug2011_53-7"><a href="#cite_note-Drug2011-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_conditions">Medical conditions</span></h3>
<p>There is an association between suicidality and physical health problems such as<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tint2010_76-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tint2010-76">[76]</a></sup> chronic pain,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> traumatic brain injury,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> cancer,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ang2012_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ang2012-114">[114]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chronic_fatigue_syndrome" title="Chronic fatigue syndrome">chronic fatigue syndrome</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> kidney failure (requiring <a href="/wiki/Hemodialysis" title="Hemodialysis">hemodialysis</a>), <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Systemic_lupus_erythematosus" title="Systemic lupus erythematosus">systemic lupus erythematosus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tint2010_76-3"><a href="#cite_note-Tint2010-76">[76]</a></sup> The diagnosis of cancer approximately doubles the subsequent frequency of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ang2012_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ang2012-114">[114]</a></sup> The prevalence of increased suicidality persisted after adjusting for depressive illness and excessive alcohol use. Among people with more than one medical condition the frequency was particularly high. In Japan, health problems are listed as the primary justification for suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup>
</p><p>Sleep disturbances, such as <a href="/wiki/Insomnia" title="Insomnia">insomnia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sleep_apnea" title="Sleep apnea">sleep apnea</a>, are risk factors for depression and suicide. In some instances, the sleep disturbances may be a risk factor independent of depression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> A number of other medical conditions may present with symptoms similar to mood disorders, including <a href="/wiki/Hypothyroidism" title="Hypothyroidism">hypothyroidism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_disease" title="Alzheimer's disease">Alzheimer's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brain_tumor" title="Brain tumor">brain tumors</a>, systemic lupus erythematosus, and adverse effects from a number of medications (such as <a href="/wiki/Beta_blocker" title="Beta blocker">beta blockers</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steroids" title="Steroids">steroids</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-9"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Occupational_factors">Occupational factors</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Suicide_in_the_military" title="Suicide in the military">Suicide in the military</a></div>
<p>Certain occupations carry an elevated risk of self-harm and suicide, such as military careers. Research in several countries has found that the rate of suicide among former armed forces personnel in particular,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:14_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-:14-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:22_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-:22-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-122">[122]</a></sup> and young veterans especially,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:14_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-:14-119">[119]</a></sup> is markedly higher than that found in the general population.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Copycat_suicide" title="Copycat suicide">Copycat suicide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_media_and_suicide" title="Social media and suicide">Social media and suicide</a></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lotte_an_Werthers_Grabmal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="743" data-file-width="891" decoding="async" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lotte_an_Werthers_Grabmal.jpg/310px-Lotte_an_Werthers_Grabmal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lotte_an_Werthers_Grabmal.jpg/465px-Lotte_an_Werthers_Grabmal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Lotte_an_Werthers_Grabmal.jpg/620px-Lotte_an_Werthers_Grabmal.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lotte_an_Werthers_Grabmal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_von_Goethe" title="Johann Wolfgang von Goethe">Goethe</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sorrows_of_Young_Werther" title="The Sorrows of Young Werther">The Sorrows of Young Werther</a></i>, the title character kills himself due to a love triangle involving Charlotte (pictured at his grave). Some admirers of the story were triggered into <a href="/wiki/Copycat_suicide" title="Copycat suicide">copycat suicide</a>, known as the "Werther effect".</div></div></div>
<p>The media, including the Internet, plays an important role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hawton2012_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hawton2012-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ocon2014_88-5"><a href="#cite_note-Ocon2014-88">[88]</a></sup> Certain depictions of suicide may increase its occurrence, with high-volume, prominent, repetitive coverage glorifying or romanticizing suicide having the most impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boh2012_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boh2012-125">[125]</a></sup> When detailed descriptions of how to kill oneself by a specific means are portrayed, this method of suicide can be imitated in vulnerable people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yip2012_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yip2012-16">[16]</a></sup> This phenomenon has been observed in several cases after press coverage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> In a bid to reduce the adverse effect of media portrayals concerning suicide report, one of the effective methods is to educate journalists on how to report suicide news in a manner that might reduce that possibility of imitation and encourage those at risk to seek for help. When journalists follow certain reporting guidelines the risk of suicides can be decreased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boh2012_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-Boh2012-125">[125]</a></sup> Getting buy-in from the media industry, however, can be difficult, especially in the long term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boh2012_125-2"><a href="#cite_note-Boh2012-125">[125]</a></sup>
</p><p>This trigger of suicide contagion or <a href="/wiki/Copycat_suicide" title="Copycat suicide">copycat suicide</a> is known as the "Werther effect", named after the protagonist in <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_von_Goethe" title="Johann Wolfgang von Goethe">Goethe</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sorrows_of_Young_Werther" title="The Sorrows of Young Werther">The Sorrows of Young Werther</a></i> who killed himself and then was emulated by many admirers of the book.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sia2012_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sia2012-128">[128]</a></sup> This risk is greater in adolescents who may romanticize death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> It appears that while news media has a significant effect, that of the entertainment media is equivocal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> It is unclear if searching for information about suicide on the Internet relates to the risk of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> The opposite of the Werther effect is the proposed "Papageno effect", in which coverage of effective coping mechanisms may have a protective effect. The term is based upon a character in <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Mozart</a>'s opera <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Flute" title="The Magic Flute">The Magic Flute</a></i>—fearing the loss of a loved one, he had planned to kill himself until his friends helped him out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sia2012_128-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sia2012-128">[128]</a></sup> As a consequence, fictional portrayals of suicide, showing alternative consequences or negative consequences, might have a preventive effect,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> for instance fiction might normalize mental health problems and encourage help-seeking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_factors">Other factors</span></h3>
<p>Trauma is a risk factor for suicidality in both children<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Port2017_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Port2017-135">[135]</a></sup> and adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ocon2014_88-6"><a href="#cite_note-Ocon2014-88">[88]</a></sup> Some may take their own lives to escape <a href="/wiki/Bullying" title="Bullying">bullying</a> or <a href="/wiki/Prejudice" title="Prejudice">prejudice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cox2012_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cox2012-136">[136]</a></sup> A history of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Childhood_sexual_abuse" title="Childhood sexual abuse">childhood sexual abuse</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> and time spent in <a href="/wiki/Foster_care" title="Foster care">foster care</a> are also risk factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Sexual abuse is believed to contribute to approximately 20% of the overall risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brent2008_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brent2008-60">[60]</a></sup> Significant adversity early in life has a negative effect on problem-solving skills and memory, both of which are implicated in suicidality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tur2016_36-5"><a href="#cite_note-Tur2016-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Problem_gambling" title="Problem gambling">Problem gambling</a> is associated with increased suicidal ideation and attempts compared to the general population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Between 12 and 24% of pathological gamblers attempt suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oliv2008_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oliv2008-140">[140]</a></sup> The rate of suicide among their spouses is three times greater than that of the general population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oliv2008_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-Oliv2008-140">[140]</a></sup> Other factors that increase the risk in problem gamblers include concomitant mental illness, alcohol, and drug misuse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup>
</p><p>Genetics might influence rates of suicide. A family history of suicide, especially in the mother, affects children more than adolescents or adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ocon2014_88-7"><a href="#cite_note-Ocon2014-88">[88]</a></sup> Adoption studies have shown that this is the case for biological relatives, but not adopted relatives. This makes familial risk factors unlikely to be due to <a href="/wiki/Imitation" title="Imitation">imitation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tur2016_36-6"><a href="#cite_note-Tur2016-36">[36]</a></sup> Once mental disorders are accounted for, the estimated <a href="/wiki/Heritability" title="Heritability">heritability</a> rate is 36% for suicidal ideation and 17% for suicide attempts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tur2016_36-7"><a href="#cite_note-Tur2016-36">[36]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_psychology" title="Evolutionary psychology">evolutionary</a> explanation for suicide is that it may improve <a href="/wiki/Inclusive_fitness" title="Inclusive fitness">inclusive fitness</a>. This may occur if the person dying by suicide cannot have more children and takes resources away from relatives by staying alive. An objection is that deaths by healthy adolescents likely does not increase inclusive fitness. <a href="/wiki/Adaptation" title="Adaptation">Adaptation</a> to a very different ancestral environment may be maladaptive in the current one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joiner2005_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-Joiner2005-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>
</p><p>Infection by the parasite <i><a href="/wiki/Toxoplasma_gondii" title="Toxoplasma gondii">Toxoplasma gondii</a></i>, more commonly known as <a href="/wiki/Toxoplasmosis" title="Toxoplasmosis">toxoplasmosis</a>, has been linked with suicide risk. One explanation states that this is caused by altered <a href="/wiki/Neurotransmitter" title="Neurotransmitter">neurotransmitter</a> activity due to the immunological response.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tur2016_36-8"><a href="#cite_note-Tur2016-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>There appears to be a link between <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollution</a> and depression and suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid31850801_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid31850801-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rational">Rational</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:72nd_Shinbu_1945_Kamikaze.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2061" data-file-width="1686" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/72nd_Shinbu_1945_Kamikaze.jpg/180px-72nd_Shinbu_1945_Kamikaze.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/72nd_Shinbu_1945_Kamikaze.jpg/270px-72nd_Shinbu_1945_Kamikaze.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/72nd_Shinbu_1945_Kamikaze.jpg/360px-72nd_Shinbu_1945_Kamikaze.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:72nd_Shinbu_1945_Kamikaze.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Teenage recruits for Japanese <a href="/wiki/Kamikaze" title="Kamikaze">Kamikaze</a> suicide pilots in May 1945</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rational_suicide" title="Rational suicide">Rational suicide</a> is the reasoned taking of one's own life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Loue2008_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-Loue2008-144">[144]</a></sup> However, some consider suicide as never being rational.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Loue2008_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-Loue2008-144">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>Euthanasia and assisted suicide are accepted practices in a number of countries among those who have a poor quality of life without the possibility of getting better.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cal2016_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cal2016-146">[146]</a></sup> They are supported by the legal arguments for a <a href="/wiki/Right_to_die" title="Right to die">right to die</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cal2016_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cal2016-146">[146]</a></sup>
</p><p>The act of taking one's life for the benefit of others is known as <a href="/wiki/Altruistic_suicide" title="Altruistic suicide">altruistic suicide</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moody2010_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moody2010-147">[147]</a></sup> An example of this is an elder ending his or her life to leave greater amounts of food for the younger people in the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moody2010_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-Moody2010-147">[147]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Inuit#Suicide,_murder,_and_death" title="Inuit">Suicide in some Inuit cultures</a> has been seen as an act of respect, courage, or wisdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hales2012_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hales2012-148">[148]</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Suicide_attack" title="Suicide attack">suicide attack</a> is a political or religious action where an attacker carries out violence against others which they understand will result in their own death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Some suicide bombers are motivated by a desire to obtain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martyrdoms" title="Martyrdoms">martyrdoms</a> or are religiously motivated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martyr2009_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Martyr2009-59">[59]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kamikaze" title="Kamikaze">Kamikaze</a> missions were carried out as a duty to a higher cause or moral obligation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hales2012_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hales2012-148">[148]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Murder%E2%80%93suicide" title="Murder–suicide">Murder–suicide</a> is an act of <a href="/wiki/Homicide" title="Homicide">homicide</a> followed within a week by suicide of the person who carried out the act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mass_suicide" title="Mass suicide">Mass suicides</a> are often performed under <a href="/wiki/Peer_pressure" title="Peer pressure">social pressure</a> where members give up <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">autonomy</a> to a leader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> Mass suicides can take place with as few as two people, often referred to as a <a href="/wiki/Suicide_pact" title="Suicide pact">suicide pact</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> In extenuating situations where continuing to live would be intolerable, some people use suicide as a means of escape.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> Some inmates in <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">Nazi concentration camps</a> are known to have killed themselves during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocaust" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a> by deliberately touching the electrified fences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Methods">Methods</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2010_suicide_rates_-_gun_versus_non-gun_-_high-income_countries.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="921" data-file-width="718" decoding="async" height="385" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/2010_suicide_rates_-_gun_versus_non-gun_-_high-income_countries.png/300px-2010_suicide_rates_-_gun_versus_non-gun_-_high-income_countries.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/2010_suicide_rates_-_gun_versus_non-gun_-_high-income_countries.png/450px-2010_suicide_rates_-_gun_versus_non-gun_-_high-income_countries.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/2010_suicide_rates_-_gun_versus_non-gun_-_high-income_countries.png/600px-2010_suicide_rates_-_gun_versus_non-gun_-_high-income_countries.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2010_suicide_rates_-_gun_versus_non-gun_-_high-income_countries.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Deaths by gun-related suicide versus non-gun-related suicide rates per 100,000 in high-income countries in 2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AJM201603_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-AJM201603-156">[156]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Suicide_methods" title="Suicide methods">Suicide methods</a></div>
<p>The leading method of suicide varies among countries. The leading methods in different regions include <a href="/wiki/Hanging" title="Hanging">hanging</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pesticide_poisoning" title="Pesticide poisoning">pesticide poisoning</a>, and firearms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aj2008_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Aj2008-17">[17]</a></sup> These differences are believed to be in part due to availability of the different methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yip2012_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-Yip2012-16">[16]</a></sup> A review of 56 countries found that hanging was the most common method in most of the countries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aj2008_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Aj2008-17">[17]</a></sup> accounting for 53% of male suicides and 39% of female suicides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup>
</p><p>Worldwide, 30% of suicides are estimated to occur from pesticide poisoning, most of which occur in the developing world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2016_2-7"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2016-2">[2]</a></sup> The use of this method varies markedly from 4% in Europe to more than 50% in the Pacific region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> It is also common in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> due to the ease of access within the farming populations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yip2012_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-Yip2012-16">[16]</a></sup> In many countries, drug overdoses account for approximately 60% of suicides among women and 30% among men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Many are unplanned and occur during an acute period of <a href="/wiki/Ambivalence" title="Ambivalence">ambivalence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yip2012_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-Yip2012-16">[16]</a></sup> The death rate varies by method: firearms 80–90%, drowning 65–80%, hanging 60–85%, jumping 35–60%, <a href="/wiki/Charcoal-burning_suicide" title="Charcoal-burning suicide">charcoal burning</a> 40–50%, pesticides 60–75%, and medication overdose 1.5–4.0%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yip2012_16-5"><a href="#cite_note-Yip2012-16">[16]</a></sup> The most common attempted methods of suicide differ from the most common methods of completion; up to 85% of attempts are via drug overdose in the developed world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tint2010_76-4"><a href="#cite_note-Tint2010-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p>In China, the consumption of pesticides is the most common method.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WRVp196_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-WRVp196-160">[160]</a></sup> In Japan, self-disembowelment known as <a href="/wiki/Seppuku" title="Seppuku">seppuku</a> (<i>harakiri</i>) still occurs;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WRVp196_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-WRVp196-160">[160]</a></sup> however, hanging and jumping are the most common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Jumping to one's death is common in both Hong Kong and Singapore at 50% and 80% respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yip2012_16-6"><a href="#cite_note-Yip2012-16">[16]</a></sup> In Switzerland, firearms are the most frequent suicide method in young males, although this method has decreased since guns have become less common.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> In the United States, 50% of suicides involve the use of firearms, with this method being somewhat more common in men (56%) than women (31%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-164">[164]</a></sup> The next most common cause was hanging in males (28%) and self-poisoning in females (31%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-164">[164]</a></sup> Together, hanging and poisoning constituted about 42% of U.S. suicides (as of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Suicide&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_164-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-164">[164]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pathophysiology">Pathophysiology</span></h2>
<p>There is no known unifying underlying <a href="/wiki/Pathophysiology" title="Pathophysiology">pathophysiology</a> for suicide;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-10"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> it is believed to result from an interplay of behavioral, socio-economic and psychological factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yip2012_16-7"><a href="#cite_note-Yip2012-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>Low levels of <a href="/wiki/Brain-derived_neurotrophic_factor" title="Brain-derived neurotrophic factor">brain-derived neurotrophic factor</a> (BDNF) are both directly associated with suicide<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> and indirectly associated through its role in major depression, posttraumatic stress disorder, schizophrenia and <a href="/wiki/Obsessive%E2%80%93compulsive_disorder" title="Obsessive–compulsive disorder">obsessive–compulsive disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Autopsy" title="Autopsy">Post-mortem</a> studies have found reduced levels of BDNF in the <a href="/wiki/Hippocampus" title="Hippocampus">hippocampus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prefrontal_cortex" title="Prefrontal cortex">prefrontal cortex</a>, in those with and without psychiatric conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Serotonin" title="Serotonin">Serotonin</a>, a brain <a href="/wiki/Neurotransmitter" title="Neurotransmitter">neurotransmitter</a>, is believed to be low in those who die by suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> This is partly based on evidence of increased levels of <a href="/wiki/5-HT2A_receptor" title="5-HT2A receptor">5-HT2A receptors</a> found after death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dwi2012_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dwi2012-169">[169]</a></sup> Other evidence includes reduced levels of a breakdown product of serotonin, <a href="/wiki/5-Hydroxyindoleacetic_acid" title="5-Hydroxyindoleacetic acid">5-hydroxyindoleacetic acid</a>, in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cerebral_spinal_fluid" title="Cerebral spinal fluid">cerebral spinal fluid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> However, direct evidence is hard to obtain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dwi2012_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dwi2012-169">[169]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Epigenetics" title="Epigenetics">Epigenetics</a>, the study of changes in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genetic_expression" title="Genetic expression">genetic expression</a> in response to <a href="/wiki/Environmental_factor" title="Environmental factor">environmental factors</a> which do not alter the underlying <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a>, is also believed to play a role in determining suicide risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prevention">Prevention</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Suicide_prevention" title="Suicide prevention">Suicide prevention</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:436px;max-width:436px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:216px;max-width:216px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:142px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image"
