//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Suicide_prevention_sign_on_the_Golden_Gate_Bridge_2.jpg/428px-Suicide_prevention_sign_on_the_Golden_Gate_Bridge_2.jpg 2x" width="214"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:216px;max-width:216px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:142px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crisis_Counseling_at_Golden_Gate_Bridge.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Crisis_Counseling_at_Golden_Gate_Bridge.jpg/214px-Crisis_Counseling_at_Golden_Gate_Bridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Crisis_Counseling_at_Golden_Gate_Bridge.jpg/321px-Crisis_Counseling_at_Golden_Gate_Bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Crisis_Counseling_at_Golden_Gate_Bridge.jpg/428px-Crisis_Counseling_at_Golden_Gate_Bridge.jpg 2x" width="214"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flow-root"><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:left/right/center;background-color:">As a <a href="/wiki/Suicide_prevention" title="Suicide prevention">suicide prevention</a> initiative, these signs on the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Bridge" title="Golden Gate Bridge">Golden Gate Bridge</a> promote a special telephone that connects to a crisis hotline, as well as a 24/7 crisis text line.</div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Troms%C3%B8brua_suicide_prevention_fence_2008-06-28_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2869" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Troms%C3%B8brua_suicide_prevention_fence_2008-06-28_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Troms%C3%B8brua_suicide_prevention_fence_2008-06-28_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Troms%C3%B8brua_suicide_prevention_fence_2008-06-28_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Troms%C3%B8brua_suicide_prevention_fence_2008-06-28_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Troms%C3%B8brua_suicide_prevention_fence_2008-06-28_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Troms%C3%B8brua_suicide_prevention_fence_2008-06-28_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Troms%C3%B8brua_suicide_prevention_fence_2008-06-28_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A suicide prevention fence on a bridge</div></div></div>
<p>Suicide prevention is a term used for the collective efforts to reduce the incidence of suicide through preventive measures. Protective factors for suicide include support, and access to therapy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cdc.gov_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-cdc.gov-52">[52]</a></sup> About 60% of people with suicidal thoughts do not seek help.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-172">[172]</a></sup> Reasons for not doing so include low perceived need, and wanting to deal with the problem alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-172">[172]</a></sup> Despite these high rates, there are few established treatments available for suicidal behavior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ocon2014_88-8"><a href="#cite_note-Ocon2014-88">[88]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Suicide_prevention#Lethal_means_reduction" title="Suicide prevention">Reducing access to certain methods</a>, such as firearms or toxins such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opioids" title="Opioids">opioids</a> and pesticides, can reduce risk of suicide by that method.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yip2012_16-8"><a href="#cite_note-Yip2012-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2012_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2012-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zal2016_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-Zal2016-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tur2016_36-9"><a href="#cite_note-Tur2016-36">[36]</a></sup> This may be in part because suicide is often an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Impulsive_(behavior)" title="Impulsive (behavior)">impulsive</a> decision, with up to 70% of near-fatal suicide attempts made after less than one hour of deliberation—thus, reducing access to easily-accessible methods of suicide may make impulsive attempts less likely to succeed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Other measures include reducing access to charcoal (for burning) and adding barriers on bridges and subway platforms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yip2012_16-9"><a href="#cite_note-Yip2012-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zal2016_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-Zal2016-15">[15]</a></sup> Treatment of drug and alcohol addiction, depression, and those who have attempted suicide in the past, may also be effective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2012_173-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2012-173">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zal2016_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-Zal2016-15">[15]</a></sup> Some have proposed reducing access to alcohol as a preventive strategy (such as reducing the number of bars).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Drug2011_53-8"><a href="#cite_note-Drug2011-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>In young adults who have recently thought about suicide, <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_behavioral_therapy" title="Cognitive behavioral therapy">cognitive behavioral therapy</a> appears to improve outcomes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ocon2014_88-9"><a href="#cite_note-Ocon2014-88">[88]</a></sup> School-based programs that increase <a href="/wiki/Mental_health_literacy" title="Mental health literacy">mental health literacy</a> and train staff have shown mixed results on suicide rates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zal2016_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-Zal2016-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">Economic development</a> through its ability to reduce poverty may be able to decrease suicide rates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stark2011_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stark2011-94">[94]</a></sup> Efforts to increase <a href="/wiki/Social_connection" title="Social connection">social connection</a>, especially in elderly males, may be effective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> In people who have attempted suicide, following up on them might prevent repeat attempts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Crisis_hotline" title="Crisis hotline">crisis hotlines</a> are common, there is little evidence to support or refute their effectiveness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sak2011_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sak2011-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zal2016_15-6"><a href="#cite_note-Zal2016-15">[15]</a></sup> Preventing childhood trauma provides an opportunity for suicide prevention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Port2017_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-Port2017-135">[135]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Suicide_Prevention_Day" title="World Suicide Prevention Day">World Suicide Prevention Day</a> is observed annually on September 10 with the support of the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_for_Suicide_Prevention" title="International Association for Suicide Prevention">International Association for Suicide Prevention</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Screening">Screening</span></h3>
<p>There is little data on the effects of screening the general population on the ultimate rate of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> Screening those who come to the emergency departments with injuries from self-harm have been shown to help identify suicide ideation and suicide intention. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychometric_tests" title="Psychometric tests">Psychometric tests</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Beck_Depression_Inventory" title="Beck Depression Inventory">Beck Depression Inventory</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Geriatric_Depression_Scale" title="Geriatric Depression Scale">Geriatric Depression Scale</a> for older people are being used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meier_2008_169_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-Meier_2008_169-182">[182]</a></sup> As there is a high rate of people who test positive via these tools that are not at risk of suicide, there are concerns that screening may significantly increase mental health care resource utilization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> Assessing those at high risk, though, is recommended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-11"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> Asking about suicidality does not appear to increase the risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-12"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mental_illness_2">Mental illness</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Antidepressants_and_suicide_risk" title="Antidepressants and suicide risk">Antidepressants and suicide risk</a></div>
<p>In those with mental health problems, a number of treatments may reduce the risk of suicide. Those who are actively suicidal may be admitted to psychiatric care either voluntarily or involuntarily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-13"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> Possessions that may be used to harm oneself are typically removed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tint2010_76-5"><a href="#cite_note-Tint2010-76">[76]</a></sup> Some clinicians get patients to sign <a href="/wiki/Suicide_prevention_contract" title="Suicide prevention contract">suicide prevention contracts</a> where they agree to not harm themselves if released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-14"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> However, evidence does not support a significant effect from this practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-15"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> If a person is at low risk, outpatient mental health treatment may be arranged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tint2010_76-6"><a href="#cite_note-Tint2010-76">[76]</a></sup> Short-term hospitalization has not been found to be more effective than community care for improving outcomes in those with borderline personality disorder who are chronically suicidal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is tentative evidence that <a href="/wiki/Psychotherapy" title="Psychotherapy">psychotherapy</a>, specifically <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dialectical_behaviour_therapy" title="Dialectical behaviour therapy">dialectical behaviour therapy</a>, reduces suicidality in adolescents<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Can2010_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-Can2010-186">[186]</a></sup> as well as in those with borderline personality disorder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> It may also be useful in decreasing suicide attempts in adults at high risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> However, a decrease in suicide has not been observed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Can2010_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-Can2010-186">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is controversy around the benefit-versus-harm of <a href="/wiki/Antidepressant" title="Antidepressant">antidepressants</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hawton2012_51-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hawton2012-51">[51]</a></sup> In young persons, some antidepressants, such as <a href="/wiki/Selective_serotonin_reuptake_inhibitor" title="Selective serotonin reuptake inhibitor">SSRIs</a>, appear to increase the risk of suicidality from 25 per 1000 to 40 per 1000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> In older persons, however, they may decrease the risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-16"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lithium_(medication)" title="Lithium (medication)">Lithium</a> appears effective at lowering the risk in those with bipolar disorder and major depression to nearly the same levels as that of the general population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Clozapine" title="Clozapine">Clozapine</a> may decrease the thoughts of suicide in some people with schizophrenia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ketamine" title="Ketamine">Ketamine</a>, which is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dissociative_anaesthetic" title="Dissociative anaesthetic">dissociative anaesthetic</a>, seems to lower the rate of suicidal ideation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> In the United States, health professionals are legally required to take reasonable steps to try to prevent suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Epidemiology">Epidemiology</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology_of_suicide" title="Epidemiology of suicide">Epidemiology of suicide</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_suicide_rate" title="List of countries by suicide rate">List of countries by suicide rate</a></div>
<p>Approximately 1.4% of people die by suicide, a mortality rate of 11.6 per 100,000 persons per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-17"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> Suicide resulted in 842,000 deaths in 2013 up from 712,000 deaths in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GDB2013_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-GDB2013-19">[19]</a></sup> Rates of suicide have increased by 60% from the 1960s to 2012, with these increases seen primarily in the developing world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hawton2009_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-Hawton2009-3">[3]</a></sup> Globally, as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Suicide&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>/2009, suicide is the tenth leading cause of death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hawton2009_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-Hawton2009-3">[3]</a></sup> For every suicide that results in death there are between 10 and 40 attempted suicides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-18"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>Suicide rates differ significantly between countries and over time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup> As a percentage of deaths in 2008 it was: Africa 0.5%, South-East Asia 1.9%, Americas 1.2% and Europe 1.4%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-5"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup> Rates per 100,000 were: Australia 8.6, Canada 11.1, China 12.7, India 23.2, United Kingdom 7.6, United States 11.4 and South Korea 28.9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> It was ranked as the 10th leading cause of death in the United States in 2016 with about 45,000 cases that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2018Epi_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDC2018Epi-198">[198]</a></sup> Rates have <a href="/wiki/Suicide_in_the_United_States" title="Suicide in the United States">increased in the United States</a> in the last few years,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2018Epi_198-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDC2018Epi-198">[198]</a></sup> with the highest value being in 2017 (the most recent data).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> In the United States, about 650,000 people are seen in emergency departments yearly due to attempting suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-19"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> The United States rate among men in their 50s rose by nearly half in the decade 1999–2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> Greenland, Lithuania, Japan, and Hungary have the highest rates of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-6"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup> Around 75% of suicides occur in the developing world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2016_2-8"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2016-2">[2]</a></sup> The countries with the greatest absolute numbers of suicides are China and India, partly due to their large population size, accounting for over half the total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-7"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup> In China, suicide is the 5th leading cause of death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China2009_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-China2009-201">[201]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 355px"><div style="width: 355px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sex_and_gender">Sex and gender</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gender_differences_in_suicide" title="Gender differences in suicide">Gender differences in suicide</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:508px;max-width:508px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Male_suicide_rates_2015_(crude).svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="231" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Male_suicide_rates_2015_%28crude%29.svg/250px-Male_suicide_rates_2015_%28crude%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Male_suicide_rates_2015_%28crude%29.svg/375px-Male_suicide_rates_2015_%28crude%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Male_suicide_rates_2015_%28crude%29.svg/500px-Male_suicide_rates_2015_%28crude%29.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Female_suicide_rates_2015_(crude).svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="230" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Female_suicide_rates_2015_%28crude%29.svg/250px-Female_suicide_rates_2015_%28crude%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Female_suicide_rates_2015_%28crude%29.svg/375px-Female_suicide_rates_2015_%28crude%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Female_suicide_rates_2015_%28crude%29.svg/500px-Female_suicide_rates_2015_%28crude%29.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Suicide rates per 100,000 males (left) and females (right).
<div>

<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#f0c809; color:black;"> </span> 5 – 10</div>

<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#f05c0d; color:black;"> </span> 15 – 25</div>

<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#cd281b; color:white;"> </span> 25 – 35</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#b00507; color:white;"> </span> Above 35</div>
</td>
<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#d1d1d1; color:black;"> </span> No data</div>
<p>
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Globally as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Suicide&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, death by suicide occurs about 1.8 times more often in males than females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-8"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a>, males die three to four times more often by means of suicide than do females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-9"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup> This difference is even more pronounced in those over the age of 65, with tenfold more males than females dying by suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sue2012_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sue2012-205">[205]</a></sup> Suicide attempts and self-harm are between two and four times more frequent among females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-20"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> Researchers have attributed the difference between suicide and attempted suicide among the sexes to males using more lethal means to end their lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sue2012_205-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sue2012-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kumar_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kumar-208">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ellis_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ellis-209">[209]</a></sup> However, separating intentional suicide attempts from non-suicidal self-harm is not currently done in places like the United States when gathering statistics at the national level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup>
</p><p>China has one of the highest female suicide rates in the world and is the only country where it is higher than that of men (ratio of 0.9).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-10"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China2009_201-1"><a href="#cite_note-China2009-201">[201]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean" title="Eastern Mediterranean">Eastern Mediterranean</a>, suicide rates are nearly equivalent between males and females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-11"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup> The highest rate of female suicide is found in South Korea at 22 per 100,000, with high rates in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">South-East Asia</a> and the Western Pacific generally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-12"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>A number of reviews have found an increased risk of suicide among <a href="/wiki/Lesbian" title="Lesbian">lesbian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gay_men" title="Gay men">gay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bisexuality" title="Bisexuality">bisexual</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Among transgender persons, rates of attempted suicide are about 40% compared to a general population rate of 5%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> This is believed to in part be due to <a href="/wiki/Transgender_inequality" title="Transgender inequality">social stigmatisation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Age">Age</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Suicide_rates_by_age,_OWID.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="850" decoding="async" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Suicide_rates_by_age%2C_OWID.svg/350px-Suicide_rates_by_age%2C_OWID.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Suicide_rates_by_age%2C_OWID.svg/525px-Suicide_rates_by_age%2C_OWID.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Suicide_rates_by_age%2C_OWID.svg/700px-Suicide_rates_by_age%2C_OWID.svg.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Suicide_rates_by_age,_OWID.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Suicide rates by age<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In many countries, the rate of suicide is highest in the middle-aged<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pit2012_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pit2012-217">[217]</a></sup> or elderly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yip2012_16-10"><a href="#cite_note-Yip2012-16">[16]</a></sup> The absolute number of suicides, however, is greatest in those between 15 and 29 years old, due to the number of people in this age group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-13"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup> Worldwide, the average age of suicide is between age 30 and 49 for both men and women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2018Age_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2018Age-218">[218]</a></sup> This means that half of people who died by suicide were approximately age 40 or younger, and half were older.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2018Age_218-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2018Age-218">[218]</a></sup> Suicidality is rare in children, but increases during the transition to adolescence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United States, the suicide death rate is greatest in Caucasian men older than 80 years, even though younger people more frequently attempt suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2011_22-21"><a href="#cite_note-EB2011-22">[22]</a></sup> It is the second most common cause of death in adolescents<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hawton2012_51-3"><a href="#cite_note-Hawton2012-51">[51]</a></sup> and in young males is second only to accidental death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pit2012_217-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pit2012-217">[217]</a></sup> In young males in the developed world, it is the cause of nearly 30% of mortality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pit2012_217-2"><a href="#cite_note-Pit2012-217">[217]</a></sup> In the developing world rates are similar, but it makes up a smaller proportion of overall deaths due to higher rates of death from other types of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trauma_(medicine)" title="Trauma (medicine)">trauma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pit2012_217-3"><a href="#cite_note-Pit2012-217">[217]</a></sup> In South-East Asia, in contrast to other areas of the world, deaths from suicide occur at a greater rate in young females than elderly females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Var2012_6-14"><a href="#cite_note-Var2012-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_suicide" title="History of suicide">History of suicide</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ludovisi_Gaul_Altemps_Inv8608_n3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2200" data-file-width="1450" decoding="async" height="440" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Ludovisi_Gaul_Altemps_Inv8608_n3.jpg/290px-Ludovisi_Gaul_Altemps_Inv8608_n3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Ludovisi_Gaul_Altemps_Inv8608_n3.jpg/435px-Ludovisi_Gaul_Altemps_Inv8608_n3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Ludovisi_Gaul_Altemps_Inv8608_n3.jpg/580px-Ludovisi_Gaul_Altemps_Inv8608_n3.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ludovisi_Gaul_Altemps_Inv8608_n3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Ludovisi_Gaul" title="Ludovisi Gaul">Ludovisi Gaul</a> killing himself and his wife, Roman copy after the <a href="/wiki/Hellenistic_art" title="Hellenistic art">Hellenistic</a> original, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palazzo_Massimo_alle_Terme" title="Palazzo Massimo alle Terme">Palazzo Massimo alle Terme</a></div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Classical_Athens" title="Classical Athens">ancient Athens</a>, a person who died by suicide without the approval of the state was denied the honors of a normal burial. The person would be buried alone, on the outskirts of the city, without a headstone or marker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> However, it was deemed to be an acceptable method to deal with military defeat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maris2000_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-Maris2000-221">[221]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Rome</a>, while suicide was initially permitted, it was later deemed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimes_against_the_state" title="Crimes against the state">crime against the state</a> due to its economic costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a> condemned all forms of suicide while <a href="/wiki/Plato" title="Plato">Plato</a> was ambivalent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Minois_Hist_Suic_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-Minois_Hist_Suic-223">[223]</a></sup> In Rome, some reasons for suicide included volunteering death in a <a href="/wiki/Gladiator" title="Gladiator">gladiator</a> combat, guilt over murdering someone, to save the life of another, as a result of mourning, from shame from being raped, and as an escape from intolerable situations like physical suffering, military defeat, or criminal pursuit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Minois_Hist_Suic_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-Minois_Hist_Suic-223">[223]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_mort_de_seneque.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="437" data-file-width="539" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/La_mort_de_seneque.jpg/220px-La_mort_de_seneque.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/La_mort_de_seneque.jpg/330px-La_mort_de_seneque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/La_mort_de_seneque.jpg/440px-La_mort_de_seneque.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_mort_de_seneque.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Death of Seneca</i> (1684), painting by <a href="/wiki/Luca_Giordano" title="Luca Giordano">Luca Giordano</a>, depicting the suicide of <a href="/wiki/Seneca_the_Younger" title="Seneca the Younger">Seneca the Younger</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Rome</a></div></div></div>
<p>Suicide came to be regarded as a <a href="/wiki/Sin" title="Sin">sin</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_Europe" title="Christian Europe">Christian Europe</a> and was condemned at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council_of_Arles_(452)" title="Council of Arles (452)">Council of Arles (452)</a> as the work of the <a href="/wiki/Devil_in_Christianity" title="Devil in Christianity">Devil</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, the Church had drawn-out discussions as to when the desire for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martyrdom" title="Martyrdom">martyrdom</a> was suicidal, as in the case of <a href="/wiki/Martyrs_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Martyrs of Córdoba">martyrs of Córdoba</a>. Despite these disputes and occasional official rulings, Catholic doctrine was not entirely settled on the subject of suicide until the later 17th century. A criminal ordinance issued by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV of France</a> in 1670 was extremely severe, even for the times: the dead person's body was drawn through the streets, face down, and then hung or thrown on a garbage heap. Additionally, all of the person's property was confiscated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maris540_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-Maris540-225">[225]</a></sup>
</p><p>Attitudes towards suicide slowly began to shift during the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>. <a href="/wiki/John_Donne" title="John Donne">John Donne</a>'s work <i><a href="/wiki/Biathanatos" title="Biathanatos">Biathanatos</a></i> contained one of the first modern defences of suicide, bringing proof from the conduct of Biblical figures, such as <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samson" title="Samson">Samson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saul" title="Saul">Saul</a>, and presenting arguments on grounds of reason and nature to sanction suicide in certain circumstances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stanf_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stanf-226">[226]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Secularization" title="Secularization">secularization</a> of society that began during the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a> questioned traditional religious attitudes (such as <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_suicide" title="Christian views on suicide">Christian views on suicide</a>) toward suicide and brought a more modern perspective to the issue. <a href="/wiki/David_Hume" title="David Hume">David Hume</a> denied that suicide was a crime as it affected no one and was potentially to the advantage of the individual. In his 1777 <i>Essays on Suicide and the Immortality of the Soul</i> he rhetorically asked, "Why should I prolong a miserable existence, because of some frivolous advantage which the public may perhaps receive from me?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stanf_226-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stanf-226">[226]</a></sup> Hume's analysis was criticized by philosopher Philip Reed as being "uncharacteristically (for him) bad", since Hume took an unusually narrow conception of duty and his conclusion depended upon the suicide producing no harm to others – including causing no grief, feelings of guilt, or emotional pain to any surviving friends and family – which is almost never the case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-227">[227]</a></sup> A shift in public opinion at large can also be discerned; <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> in 1786 initiated a spirited debate on the motion "Is suicide an act of courage?".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup>
</p><p>By the 19th century, the act of suicide had shifted from being viewed as caused by sin to being caused by <a href="/wiki/Insanity" title="Insanity">insanity</a> in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maris540_225-1"><a href="#cite_note-Maris540-225">[225]</a></sup> Although suicide remained illegal during this period, it increasingly became the target of satirical comments, such as the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Sullivan" title="Gilbert and Sullivan">Gilbert and Sullivan</a> <a href="/wiki/Comic_opera" title="Comic opera">comic opera</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mikado" title="The Mikado">The Mikado</a></i>, which satirized the idea of executing someone who had already killed himself.
</p><p>By 1879, English law began to distinguish between suicide and homicide, although suicide still resulted in forfeiture of estate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dost_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dost-229">[229]</a></sup> In 1882, the deceased were permitted daylight burial in England<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> and by the middle of the 20th century, suicide had become legal in much of the Western world. The term <i>suicide</i> first emerged shortly before 1700 to replace expressions on self-death which were often characterized as a form of self-murder in the West.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Minois_Hist_Suic_223-2"><a href="#cite_note-Minois_Hist_Suic-223">[223]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_and_culture">Social and culture</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislation">Legislation</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Suicide_legislation" title="Suicide legislation">Suicide legislation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wakisashi-sepukku-p1000699.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2300" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Wakisashi-sepukku-p1000699.jpg/220px-Wakisashi-sepukku-p1000699.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Wakisashi-sepukku-p1000699.jpg/330px-Wakisashi-sepukku-p1000699.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Wakisashi-sepukku-p1000699.jpg/440px-Wakisashi-sepukku-p1000699.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wakisashi-sepukku-p1000699.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <i><a href="/wiki/Tant%C5%8D" title="Tantō">tantō</a></i> knife prepared for <i><a href="/wiki/Seppuku" title="Seppuku">seppuku</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Abdomen" title="Abdomen">abdomen</a>-cutting)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seppuku-2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1539" data-file-width="1104" decoding="async" height="307" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Seppuku-2.jpg/220px-Seppuku-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Seppuku-2.jpg/330px-Seppuku-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Seppuku-2.jpg/440px-Seppuku-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seppuku-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">Samurai</a> about to perform seppuku</div></div></div>
<p>No country in Europe currently considers suicide or attempted suicide to be a crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McL2007_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-McL2007-231">[231]</a></sup> It was, however, in most Western European countries from the Middle Ages until at least the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dost_229-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dost-229">[229]</a></sup> The Netherlands was the first country to legalize both physician-assisted suicide and euthanasia, which took effect in 2002, although only doctors are allowed to assist in either of them, and have to follow a protocol <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia_in_the_Netherlands" title="Euthanasia in the Netherlands">prescribed by Dutch law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> If such protocol is not followed, it is an offence punishable by law. In Germany, active euthanasia is illegal and anyone present during suicide may be prosecuted for failure to render aid in an emergency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> Switzerland has taken steps to legalize assisted suicide for the chronically mentally ill. The high court in <a href="/wiki/Lausanne" title="Lausanne">Lausanne</a>, Switzerland, in a 2006 ruling, granted an anonymous individual with longstanding psychiatric difficulties the right to end his own life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid17649899_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid17649899-234">[234]</a></sup> England and Wales decriminalized suicide via the <a href="/wiki/Suicide_Act_1961" title="Suicide Act 1961">Suicide Act 1961</a> and the Republic of Ireland in 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McL2007_231-1"><a href="#cite_note-McL2007-231">[231]</a></sup> The word "commit" was used in reference to its being illegal, but many organisations have stopped it because of the negative connotation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_style_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_style-236">[236]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United States, suicide is not illegal, but may be associated with penalties for those who attempt it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McL2007_231-2"><a href="#cite_note-McL2007-231">[231]</a></sup> Physician-assisted suicide is legal in the state of <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a> for people with terminal diseases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, people with terminal diseases may request medications to help end their life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> Canadians who have attempted suicide may be barred from entering the United States. U.S. laws allow border guards to deny access to people who have a mental illness, including those with previous suicide attempts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Australia, suicide is not a crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup> However, it is a crime to counsel, incite, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aid_and_abet" title="Aid and abet">aid and abet</a> another in attempting to die by suicide, and the law explicitly allows any person to use "such force as may reasonably be necessary" to prevent another from taking their own life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a> of Australia briefly had legal physician-assisted suicide from 1996 to 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup>
</p><p>In India, suicide was illegal until 2014, and surviving family members used to face legal difficulties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> It remains a criminal offense in most Muslim-majority nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Islam2006_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-Islam2006-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_views">Religious views</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religious_views_on_suicide" title="Religious views on suicide">Religious views on suicide</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Christianity">Christianity</span></h4>
<p>Most forms of Christianity consider suicide sinful, based mainly on the writings of influential Christian thinkers of the Middle Ages, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Augustine" title="St. Augustine">St. Augustine</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Thomas_Aquinas" title="St. Thomas Aquinas">St. Thomas Aquinas</a>, but suicide was not considered a sin under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a> Christian <a href="/wiki/Code_of_Justinian" title="Code of Justinian">code of Justinian</a>, for instance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholic</a> and Orthodox doctrine, suicide is considered to be murder, violating the <a href="/wiki/Ten_Commandments" title="Ten Commandments">commandment</a> "Thou shalt not kill," and historically neither church would even hold a burial service for a member that died by suicide, deeming it an act that condemned the person to hell, since they died in a state of mortal sin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> The basic idea being that life is a gift given by God which should not be spurned, and that suicide is against the "natural order" and thus interferes with God's master plan for the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> However, it is believed that mental illness or grave fear of suffering diminishes the responsibility of the one completing suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Judaism">Judaism</span></h4>
<p>Judaism focuses on the importance of valuing this life, and as such, suicide is tantamount to denying God's goodness in the world. Despite this, under extreme circumstances when there has seemed no choice but to either be killed or forced to betray their religion, there are several accounts of Jews having died by suicide, either individually or in groups (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocaust" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masada" title="Masada">Masada</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_France#First_persecution_of_the_Jews" title="History of the Jews in France">First French persecution of the Jews</a> and <a href="/wiki/York_Castle" title="York Castle">York Castle</a> for examples), and as a grim reminder there is even a prayer in the Jewish liturgy for "when the knife is at the throat", for those dying "to sanctify God's Name" (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martyrdom" title="Martyrdom">Martyrdom</a>). These acts have received mixed responses by Jewish authorities, regarded by some as examples of heroic martyrdom, while others state that it was wrong for them to take their own lives in anticipation of martyrdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">Islam</span></h4>
<p>Islamic religious views are against suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Islam2006_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-Islam2006-29">[29]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a> forbids it by stating "do not kill or destroy yourself".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gear2009_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gear2009-252">[252]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hadith" title="Hadith">hadiths</a> also state individual suicide to be unlawful and a sin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Islam2006_29-5"><a href="#cite_note-Islam2006-29">[29]</a></sup> Stigma is often associated with suicide in Islamic countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gear2009_252-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gear2009-252">[252]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hinduism_and_Jainism">Hinduism and Jainism</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_Hindoo_Widow_Burning_Herself_with_the_Corpse_of_her_Husband.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="465" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/A_Hindoo_Widow_Burning_Herself_with_the_Corpse_of_her_Husband.jpg/220px-A_Hindoo_Widow_Burning_Herself_with_the_Corpse_of_her_Husband.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/A_Hindoo_Widow_Burning_Herself_with_the_Corpse_of_her_Husband.jpg/330px-A_Hindoo_Widow_Burning_Herself_with_the_Corpse_of_her_Husband.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/A_Hindoo_Widow_Burning_Herself_with_the_Corpse_of_her_Husband.jpg/440px-A_Hindoo_Widow_Burning_Herself_with_the_Corpse_of_her_Husband.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_Hindoo_Widow_Burning_Herself_with_the_Corpse_of_her_Husband.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> widow <a href="/wiki/Sati_(practice)" title="Sati (practice)">burning herself</a> with her husband's corpse, 1820s</div></div></div>
<p>In Hinduism, suicide is generally disdained and is considered equally sinful as murdering another in contemporary Hindu society. <a href="/wiki/Hindu_texts" title="Hindu texts">Hindu Scriptures</a> state that one who dies by suicide will become part of the spirit world, wandering earth until the time one would have otherwise died, had one not taken one's own life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> However, Hinduism accepts a man's right to end one's life through the non-violent practice of fasting to death, termed <i><a href="/wiki/Prayopavesa" title="Prayopavesa">Prayopavesa</a></i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-hindu-254">[254]</a></sup> but <i>Prayopavesa</i> is strictly restricted to people who have no desire or ambition left, and no responsibilities remaining in this life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu_254-1"><a href="#cite_note-hindu-254">[254]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a> has a similar practice named <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santhara" title="Santhara">Santhara</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Sati_(practice)" title="Sati (practice)">Sati</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Self-immolation" title="Self-immolation">self-immolation</a> by widows, is a rare and illegal practice in Hindu society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ainu">Ainu</span></h4>
<p>Within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ainu_religion" title="Ainu religion">Ainu religion</a>, someone who dies by suicide is believed to become a <a href="/wiki/Ghost" title="Ghost">ghost</a> (tukap) who would haunt the living,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yamada_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-yamada-256">[256]</a></sup> to come to fulfillment from which they were excluded during life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adami_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-adami-257">[257]</a></sup> Also, someone who insults another so they kill themselves is regarded as co-responsible for their death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adami-2_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-adami-2-258">[258]</a></sup> According to Norbert Richard Adami, this ethic exists due to the case that solidarity within the community is much more important to Ainu culture than it is to the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adami-2_258-1"><a href="#cite_note-adami-2-258">[258]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philosophy">Philosophy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_suicide" title="Philosophy of suicide">Philosophy of suicide</a></div>
<p>A number of questions are raised within the philosophy of suicide, including what constitutes suicide, whether or not suicide can be a rational choice, and the moral permissibility of suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordSuicide_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordSuicide-259">[259]</a></sup> Arguments as to acceptability of suicide in moral or social terms range from the position that the act is inherently immoral and unacceptable under any circumstances, to a regard for suicide as a sacrosanct right of anyone who believes they have rationally and conscientiously come to the decision to end their own lives, even if they are young and healthy.
</p><p>Opponents to suicide include philosophers such as <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">Augustine of Hippo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas" title="Thomas Aquinas">Thomas Aquinas</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordSuicide_259-1"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordSuicide-259">[259]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Kant" title="Immanuel Kant">Immanuel Kant</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> and, arguably, <a href="/wiki/John_Stuart_Mill" title="John Stuart Mill">John Stuart Mill</a> – Mill's focus on the importance of liberty and autonomy meant that he rejected choices which would prevent a person from making future autonomous decisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> Others view suicide as a legitimate matter of personal choice. Supporters of this position maintain that no one should be forced to suffer against their will, particularly from conditions such as incurable disease, mental illness, and old age, with no possibility of improvement. They reject the belief that suicide is always irrational, arguing instead that it can be a valid last resort for those enduring major pain or trauma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup> A stronger stance would argue that people should be allowed to autonomously choose to die regardless of whether they are suffering. Notable supporters of this <a href="/wiki/School_of_thought" title="School of thought">school of thought</a> include Scottish empiricist <a href="/wiki/David_Hume" title="David Hume">David Hume</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StanfordSuicide_259-2"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordSuicide-259">[259]</a></sup> who accepted suicide so long as it did not harm or violate a duty to God, other people, or the self,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_227-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-227">[227]</a></sup> and American bioethicist <a href="/wiki/Jacob_M._Appel" title="Jacob M. Appel">Jacob Appel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid17649899_234-1"><a href="#cite_note-pmid17649899-234">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Advocacy">Advocacy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Advocacy_of_suicide" title="Advocacy of suicide">Advocacy of suicide</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alexandre-Gabriel_Decamps_-_The_Suicide_-_Walters_3742.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1247" data-file-width="1799" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Alexandre-Gabriel_Decamps_-_The_Suicide_-_Walters_3742.jpg/220px-Alexandre-Gabriel_Decamps_-_The_Suicide_-_Walters_3742.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Alexandre-Gabriel_Decamps_-_The_Suicide_-_Walters_3742.jpg/330px-Alexandre-Gabriel_Decamps_-_The_Suicide_-_Walters_3742.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Alexandre-Gabriel_Decamps_-_The_Suicide_-_Walters_3742.jpg/440px-Alexandre-Gabriel_Decamps_-_The_Suicide_-_Walters_3742.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alexandre-Gabriel_Decamps_-_The_Suicide_-_Walters_3742.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In this painting by <a href="/wiki/Alexandre-Gabriel_Decamps" title="Alexandre-Gabriel Decamps">Alexandre-Gabriel Decamps</a>, the palette, pistol, and note lying on the floor suggest that the event has just taken place; an artist has taken his own life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Advocacy of suicide has occurred in many cultures and <a href="/wiki/Subculture" title="Subculture">subcultures</a>. The Japanese military during World War II encouraged and glorified kamikaze attacks, which were suicide attacks by military aviators from the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> against <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> naval vessels in the closing stages of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Theater_(World_War_II)" title="Pacific Theater (World War II)">Pacific Theater</a> of World War II. Japanese society as a whole has been described as "suicide-tolerant"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ozawa-desilva_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-ozawa-desilva-265">[265]</a></sup> (see <a href="/wiki/Suicide_in_Japan" title="Suicide in Japan">Suicide in Japan</a>).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Suicide_and_the_Internet" title="Suicide and the Internet">Internet searches for information on suicide</a> return webpages that 10–30% of the time encourage or facilitate suicide attempts. There is some concern that such sites may push those predisposed over the edge. Some people form suicide pacts online, either with pre-existing friends or people they have recently encountered in chat rooms or <a href="/wiki/Internet_forum" title="Internet forum">message boards</a>. The Internet, however, may also help prevent suicide by providing a social group for those who are isolated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dur2011_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dur2011-266">[266]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Locations">Locations</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_suicide_sites" title="List of suicide sites">List of suicide sites</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suicides_at_the_Golden_Gate_Bridge" title="Suicides at the Golden Gate Bridge">Suicides at the Golden Gate Bridge</a></div>
<p>Some landmarks have become known for high levels of suicide attempts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robinson2012_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson2012-267">[267]</a></sup> These include China's <a href="/wiki/Nanjing_Yangtze_River_Bridge" title="Nanjing Yangtze River Bridge">Nanjing Yangtze River Bridge</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> San Francisco's <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Bridge" title="Golden Gate Bridge">Golden Gate Bridge</a>, Japan's <a href="/wiki/Aokigahara" title="Aokigahara">Aokigahara Forest</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> England's <a href="/wiki/Beachy_Head" title="Beachy Head">Beachy Head</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robinson2012_267-1"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson2012-267">[267]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bloor_Street_Viaduct" title="Bloor Street Viaduct">Bloor Street Viaduct</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dennis2008_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dennis2008-270">[270]</a></sup> As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Suicide&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Golden Gate Bridge has had more than 1,300 die by suicide by jumping since its construction in 1937.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McDougall2010_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-McDougall2010-271">[271]</a></sup> Many locations where suicide is common have constructed barriers to prevent it;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bateson2008_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bateson2008-272">[272]</a></sup> this includes the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luminous_Veil" title="Luminous Veil">Luminous Veil</a> in Toronto,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dennis2008_270-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dennis2008-270">[270]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Eiffel_Tower" title="Eiffel Tower">Eiffel Tower</a> in Paris, the <a href="/wiki/West_Gate_Bridge" title="West Gate Bridge">West Gate Bridge</a> in Melbourne, and <a href="/wiki/Empire_State_Building" title="Empire State Building">Empire State Building</a> in New York City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bateson2008_272-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bateson2008-272">[272]</a></sup> They generally appear to be effective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miller2011_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miller2011-273">[273]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_cases">Notable cases</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tojo_suicide.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="619" data-file-width="802" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Tojo_suicide.jpg/220px-Tojo_suicide.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Tojo_suicide.jpg/330px-Tojo_suicide.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Tojo_suicide.jpg/440px-Tojo_suicide.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tojo_suicide.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Japanese general <a href="/wiki/Hideki_Tojo" title="Hideki Tojo">Hideki Tojo</a>, receiving treatment immediately after attempted suicide, 1945</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_suicides" title="List of suicides">List of suicides</a></div>
<p>An example of <a href="/wiki/Mass_suicide" title="Mass suicide">mass suicide</a> is the 1978 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jonestown_mass_murder/suicide" title="Jonestown mass murder/suicide">Jonestown mass murder/suicide</a> in which 909 members of the <a href="/wiki/Peoples_Temple" title="Peoples Temple">Peoples Temple</a>, an American <a href="/wiki/New_religious_movement" title="New religious movement">new religious movement</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Jones" title="Jim Jones">Jim Jones</a>, ended their lives by drinking grape <a href="/wiki/Flavor_Aid" title="Flavor Aid">Flavor Aid</a> laced with <a href="/wiki/Potassium_cyanide" title="Potassium cyanide">cyanide</a> and various prescription drugs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tape_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-tape-275">[275]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup>
</p><p>Thousands of Japanese civilians took their own lives in the last days of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Saipan" title="Battle of Saipan">Battle of Saipan</a> in 1944, some jumping from "<a href="/wiki/Suicide_Cliff" title="Suicide Cliff">Suicide Cliff</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Banzai_Cliff" title="Banzai Cliff">Banzai Cliff</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1981_Irish_hunger_strike" title="1981 Irish hunger strike">1981 Irish hunger strikes</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Sands" title="Bobby Sands">Bobby Sands</a>, resulted in 10 deaths. The cause of death was recorded by the coroner as "starvation, self-imposed" rather than suicide; this was modified to simply "starvation" on the death certificates after protest from the dead strikers' families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Philosophy59OKeeffe_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-Philosophy59OKeeffe-278">[278]</a></sup> During World War II, <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Rommel" title="Erwin Rommel">Erwin Rommel</a> was found to have foreknowledge of the <a href="/wiki/20_July_plot" title="20 July plot">July 20 plot</a> on Hitler's life; he was threatened with <a href="/wiki/Public_trial" title="Public trial">public trial</a>, execution, and reprisals on his family unless he killed himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_species">Other species</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Animal_suicide" title="Animal suicide">Animal suicide</a></div>
<p>As suicide requires a willful attempt to die, some feel it therefore cannot be said to occur in non-human animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Maris2000_221-1"><a href="#cite_note-Maris2000-221">[221]</a></sup> Suicidal behavior has been observed in <i><a href="/wiki/Salmonella" title="Salmonella">Salmonella</a></i> seeking to overcome competing bacteria by triggering an <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune system</a> response against them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup> Suicidal defenses by workers are also noted in the Brazilian ant <i><a href="/wiki/Forelius_pusillus" title="Forelius pusillus">Forelius pusillus</a></i>, where a small group of ants leaves the security of the nest after sealing the entrance from the outside each evening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pea_aphid" title="Pea aphid">Pea aphids</a>, when threatened by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ladybug" title="Ladybug">ladybug</a>, can explode themselves, scattering and protecting their brethren and sometimes even killing the ladybug; this form of suicidal <a href="/wiki/Altruism_(biology)" title="Altruism (biology)">altruism</a> is known as <a href="/wiki/Autothysis" title="Autothysis">autothysis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup> Some species of <a href="/wiki/Termite" title="Termite">termites</a> (for example <i><a href="/wiki/Globitermes_sulphureus" title="Globitermes sulphureus">Globitermes sulphureus</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-283">[283]</a></sup> have soldiers that explode, covering their enemies with sticky goo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_283-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-283">[283]</a></sup>
</p><p>There have been anecdotal reports of dogs, horses, and dolphins killing themselves,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup> but little scientific study of animal suicide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid9616791_286-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid9616791-286">[286]</a></sup> Animal suicide is usually put down to romantic human interpretation and is not generally thought to be intentional. Some of the reasons animals are thought to unintentionally kill themselves include: psychological stress, infection by certain parasites or fungi, or disruption of a long-held social tie, such as the ending of a long association with an owner and thus not accepting food from another individual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-101">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFZuckerman2007">Zuckerman P (2007).  Martin M (ed.). <i>The Cambridge Companion to Atheism</i>. Cambridge Univ. Press. pp. 58–59. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0521603676" title="Special:BookSources/978-0521603676"><bdi>978-0521603676</bdi></a>. <q>Concerning suicide rates, religious nations fare better than secular nations. According to the 2003 World Health Organization's report on international male suicides rates, of the top ten nations with the highest male suicide rates, all but one (Sri Lanka) are strongly irreligious nations with high levels of atheism. Of the top remaining nine nations leading the world in male suicide rates, all are former Soviet/Communist nations, such as Belarus, Ukraine, and Latvia. Of the bottom ten nations with the lowest male suicide rates, all are highly religious nations with statistically insignificant levels of organic atheism.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Cambridge+Companion+to+Atheism&amp;rft.pages=58-59&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+Univ.+Press&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.isbn=978-0521603676&amp;rft.aulast=Zuckerman&amp;rft.aufirst=P&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASuicide"></span></span>
